ii
==PAGE:4==
Abstract
The Danish government has stated the objective to have a 100% renewable energy supply
in all energy sections by the end of the year 2050. The large-scale ammonia heat pump
is a great candidate for fulﬁlling the objective. By combining the heat pump with low-
temperature sea water and using Sjællandsbroen’s district heating network as a heat sink,
the heat pump becomes a great tool for fulﬁlling the future goal. However, the design
of the heat exchanger conﬁguration for the heat pump for district heating can be very
time-consuming because the conﬁguration can be designed from a simple design with few
heat exchangers to a complex design with several heat exchangers.
Through numerical models in the commercial software package Engineering Equation
Solver, the thesis will optimize a 5 MW ammonia two-stage heat pump for district heating
by increasing the complexity of the district heating conﬁguration and in the meantime
vary the applied heat exchangers type from plate heat exchangers to a shell and plate heat
exchangers. In total, four combinations are studied and their coeﬃcient of performance,
district heating and pressure drop are compared. The two thermodynamically best per-
forming heat exchangers are moreover compared economically. Subsequently, sensitivity’s
analysis of the coeﬃcient of performance, the district heating area and pump power are
created for the economical best performing conﬁguration in order to better understand
the inﬂuence of the geometry and internal variables of the heat exchanger. Finally, the
sensitivity analysis is used to optimize the coeﬃcient of performance and district heating
area of the best performing heat exchanger conﬁguration.
The calculation in the thesis study shows that the coeﬃcient of performance increases
when the complexity of the heat pump increases. Moreover, the conﬁguration with the
plate heat exchangers uses a less heat transfer area, which leads to the result that it
has the lowest total capital investment. The sensitivity analysis shows that the pinch
point temperature diﬀerence, plate corrugation angle and water channel velocity have
the greatest inﬂuence of the COP and district heating area.
The optimization shows
that when the corrugation angle is 53, 66◦, the velocity is 0, 8 m/s and the pinch point
temperature diﬀerence is 2,037 K, the best design of the 5 MW large-scale ammonia HP
with plate heat exchanger is obtained, which results in a COP of 3,240 a district heating
area of 193, 48 m2 and a TCI of ¤ 3.751.756,1
Keywords: Heat pump, district heating, plate heat exchangers, shell and plate heat
exchangers, Engineering Equation Solver, pressure drops, COP optimization.
iii
==PAGE:5==
Resume
Den danske regering har angivet m˚alet om at have en 100% vedvarende energiforsyning
inden for alle energisektorer inden udgangen af 2050.
En teknologi, som kan opfylde
dette m˚al, er ammoniakvarmepumpen. Ved at kombinere varmepumpen med havvand og
benytte fjernvarmenettet ved Sjællandsbroen, kan varmepumpen blive en stærk fremtidig
løsning. Det kan dog være tidskrævende at designe en fjernvarmevekslerkonﬁguration,
idet konﬁgurationen kan designes lige fra en simpel løsning med f˚a varmevekslere til en
kompleks løsning med adskillige varmevekslerkomponenter.
Denne afhandling vil igennem numeriske modeller i programmet Engineering Equation
Solver optimere en 5 MW ammoniakvarmepumpe til fjernvarme. Dette vil ske ved at øge
kompleksiteten af varmevekslerkonﬁgurationen og samtidig variere benyttede varmevek-
slere fra pladevarmevekslere til ”shell and plate”-varmevekslere. Der vil i alt blive mod-
uleret og undersøgt ﬁre kombinationer af varmevekslere og fjernvarmekonﬁgurationer. I
undersøgelsen vil ”COP”, det samlede varmevekslerareal samt trykfaldet over de forskel-
lige varmevekslerne blive undersøgt. De to bedste kombinationer vil ydermere blive valid-
eret økonomisk. Efterfølgende vil en følsomhedsanalyse undersøge, hvilke geometriske og
interne variabler, som har størst indﬂydelse p˚a ”COP”, fjernvarmeareal og pumpearbejde
for den best økonomiske performende kombination. Afslutningsvis vil resultaterne fra
følsomhedsanalysen blive anvendt til at optimere COP og fjernvarmearealet af den bedste
kombination af varmeveksler og fjernvarmekonﬁguration.
Resultaterne af denne afhandling viser, at COP forbedres markant, n˚ar kompleksiteten
af varmevekslerkonﬁgurationen forøges. Ydermere benytter pladevarmeveksleren et min-
dre fjernvarmeareal end ”shell and plate”-varmeveksleren grundet at dens varmeoverførings
- koeﬃcienter er større. Dette medfører ogs˚a, at varmepumpekonﬁgurationen med plade-
varmeveksler har lavest TCI-værdi.
Følsomhedsanalysen viser yderligere, at de tre variabler, som har størst indﬂydelse p˚a
fjernvarmearealet og COP er; ”corrugation angle”, pinch point temperaturen samt vand-
hastigheden i varmevekslerne. En optimering viser, at n˚ar corrugation angle er 53, 66◦,
hastigheden er 0,8 m/s og temperaturen er 2,037 K opn˚as den bedste COP løsning for
den undersøgt ammoniak varmepumpe, da COP bliver 3,240 varmevekslerareal bliver
193, 48 m2 og TCI bliver ¤ 3.751.756,1
Nøgleord: Varmepumpe, fjernvarmeareal, pladevarmeveksler, shell and plate varme
- veksler, Enginering Equation Solver, tryktab, COP optimmering.

This thesis presents my ﬁnal assignment in order to achieve a master degree in mechanical
engineering within the focus area of thermal engineering at the Technical University of
Denmark.
The project was supervised by Brian Elmegaard from the section of Thermal Energy
at DTU, whom I came in contact with by attending one of his courses. I would like to
thank him for his excellent and inspiring guidance and support, which has been a great
help during the thesis study.
I would moreover like to thank my two co-supervisors Torben Schmidt Ommen and
Pernille Hartmund Jørgensen, who both have been a great resource to accessing materials
and professional assistance during the project.
Kgs. Lyngby, 4th June 2019
Christian Koch Jensen

==PAGE:16==
Chapter 1
Introduction
Through the last decade, a still increasing focus has been on the environment in Denmark,
and many people wish Denmark to become a leading pioneer within the green energy
section. In order to accomplish this goal, the Danish government has stated the objective
to have a 100% renewable supply of electricity and heating by 2035 and a 100% renewable
energy supply in all energy sections by the end of year 2050 [1].
In Figure (1.1) the
statistics of the Danish energy sources from 1990 until 2018 is presented. Here it can
be seen that crude oil and natural gas have topped in 2005.
From 2005 until 2018,
the renewable energy has slowly increased. But the Danish people still rely on energy
production which utilizes crude oil and waste as energy source. So there is still a long
way to go if the Danish energy goal shall be reached by the end of 2050.
0
200
400
600
800
1000
1200
1400
1990
2000
2005
2010

Crude Oil

Figure 1.1: Energy sources in Denmark from 1990 to 2018. The x-axis is given in years
and the y-axis is given in petajoule [2].
1
==PAGE:17==
In Denmark, we are surrounded by almost unlimited low temperature energy sources
such as sewage and sea water. An old technology which may fulﬁll Denmark’s energy
goals and utilize this ”free” energy sources is the heat pump (HP). By connecting the HP
cycle to district heating system (DH) and using sea water or sew water as low temperature
heat source, the HP becomes a strong candidate for the future renewable energy market.
Back in the 90’s, the HP was allowed to use the synthetic CFC (Fully Halogenated
Hydrocarbons) refrigerants such as R12 (Freon). However, after discovering that R12 was
highly Ozon Depletion Potential (ODP), it was banned in Denmark after 1st January1996
[3]. Instead HFC (Partly Halogenated Hydrocarbons) refrigerants such as R134a were used
until it got partly banned in Denmark after 1st January 1997 because the refrigerant was
global warming potently (GWP) and contributed to the green house eﬀect. In order to
avoid ODP and GWP, natural refrigerants such as ammonia (R717) and carbon dioxide
(R744) have been used as an alternative refrigerant up to this date.
Today HP using natural refrigerant and low temperature heat sources are starting to
appear into the Danish heating market as small HP plants connected to DH networks.
But if Denmark’s future energy goals shall be reached, it is necessary to up-scale this
HP to large-scale HP. In order to do so, much testing and studying of diﬀerent DH
conﬁgurations must be performed. However, the heat exchanger conﬁguration for HP for
DH can be designed in many ways from a simple to a complex systems. Moreover, many
diﬀerent types of heat exchangers (HEX) can be used. This makes it hard to choose the
most energy and cost optimal design. So there is a need for studying how HP behaves
thermodynamically as well as economically when various HEX types are applied to the
HP for DH system with increasing complexity.
2
==PAGE:18==
1.1
Background
The overall goal of this thesis is to theoretically optimize a large-scale HP for DH, thermo-
dynamically as well as economically. This will be done by applying diﬀerent HEX types
to a large-scale HP and in the meantime increase the complexity of the DH conﬁguration.
Additionally, the thesis will investigate what inﬂuence the HEX pressure drops have on
the coeﬃcient of performance (COP). Finally, the thesis will study what inﬂuence HEX
variables have on the COP and DH area.
The design of the large-scale HP for the diﬀerent DH conﬁgurations will take inspira-
tion from two already existing HPs which utilize low-temperature seawater and ground-
water as heat sources and is connected to a DH network. The ﬁrst HP is from the project
called ”SVAF” (large heat pumps for district heating). The SVAF project was created
after the three major Danish utility companies; HOFOR, CTR and VEKS joined forces.
The aim of SVAF is to accelerate the use of large HP’s for DH plus to test various heat
sources with suﬃcient energy potential for supplying greater Copenhagen with heat. The
three companies have established a demo of a 5 MW large-scale ammonia HP at Sjæl-
landsbroen in Copenhagen. During the thesis study, the SVAF HP was visited and a
better understanding of how the HP work was obtained. In Figure (1.2), a picture of the
SVAF HP is presented.
Figure 1.2: Inside the SVAF HP at Sjællandsbroen in Copenhagen [4].
3
==PAGE:19==
In Figure (1.3), a PI-diagram of the SVAF HP is presented. The HP consists of a
lower and an upper HP cycle, each operating at low and high pressure stage. The HP
extracts heat from sewage and sea water and raises the temperature of DH water from
50 ◦C to 80 ◦C [5].
Figure 1.3: PI-diagram of the SVAF HP in Copenhagen [5].
The second HP is from the project called ”FLEXHEAT” and is built by Johnson
Control [6]. The HP has a capacity of 800 kW and consists of a single HP with two pressure
stages. The HP is capable of supplying hot water to three cruise ships terminals and
UNICEF’s high-rack warehouse in Nordhavnen. The HP extracts heat from groundwater
bore holes and raises the temperature of the DH water to 75◦C [6].
The SVAF HP and FLEXHEAT HP are similar in many ways. They almost have the
same forward temperature and are both two pressure-stage cycles. However, the SVAF
HP only uses plate heat exchangers (PHEX) whereas the FLEXHEAT HP uses a variety
of PHEX and shell and plate heat exchangers (SPHEX). As these two HEX types seem
to be the ones most used in the DH conﬁgurations, they were chosen for the study of
diﬀerent DH conﬁgurations in the thesis.
4
==PAGE:20==
In the thesis, the HP of modeling for the diﬀerent DH conﬁgurations will have the
basic design presented in Figure (1.4).
Figure 1.4: PI-diagram of the basic HP of simulations. The HP is divided into a grid
showing the low and high pressure stage for HP 1 and HP 2.
The HP will utilize sea water as low temperature heat source and use the DH network
at Sjællandsbroen as a heat sink. The HP of modeling consists of a lower and upper
HP (HP 1 and HP 2) each operating at a low and a high pressure stage. The HP has
many similarities with the SVAF HP. However, in order to study the eﬀect of the DH
complexity, the DH conﬁguration from the SVAF has been redesigned, so it is connected
in series over the two condenser units consisting of a set of: desuperheater, condenser and
subcooler. The heat load of the HP will be 5 MW as in the SVAF project. The heat load
5
==PAGE:21==
will be distributed equally 50-50% over HP 1 and HP 2 heat sinks. Moreover, the same
return and forward values as in the SVAF project will be used, see Table (1.1).
Table 1.1: Input and output values for the 5 MW HP of modeling.

The two HP cycles will use the ﬂuid R717 (ammonia) as refrigerant. For the sea water
and DH water, the ﬂuid H2O will be used. Finally, a pinch point temperature diﬀerence
∆Tpinch of 5 K will be used for all the HEXs.
In overall, the thesis will study two HEX types; plate heat exchanger (PHEX) and
shell and plate heat exchanger (SPHEX) for two diﬀerent DH conﬁgurations. The two
conﬁgurations will be called ”Design 1” and ”Design 2”. Design 1 will have a setup as
presented in Figure (1.4) where the two condenser units are in series. Design 2 will utilize
the heat after compressor 1 and 3 by applying two desuperheaters (DSHL and DSHH).
Design 1 and Design 2 will be explained in more detail at the beginning of the method
section. In total, there will be four design combinations; Design 1 with PHEX, Design 1
with SPHEX, Design 2 with PHEX and Design 2 with SPHEX, see Figure (1.5).
Figure 1.5: Matrix showing the four combinations of HEX and DH conﬁgurations.
6
==PAGE:22==
By analyzing these four combinations, it is possible to obtain a better understanding
of how the choice of HEX and complexity of DH conﬁguration will aﬀect the HP and how
an optimization of the HP can be performed thermodynamically as well economically.
Moreover, by analyzing the diﬀerent HEX types, a better understanding of what inﬂuence
the pressure drops will have on the COP and how important it is to include them in the
HP modeling. Finally, the analysis of the HEX will also give a better picture of how the
COP best can be optimized and how the DH area best can be minimized when the HEX
geometry and internal variables are changed.
1.2
Problem statement
Is it possible to theoretically optimize a heat exchanger conﬁguration for a 5 MW ammo-
nia two-stage heat pump for district heating in Copenhagen by increasing the complexity
of the district heating conﬁguration and varying the HEX type used in the system? More-
over, how can the coeﬃcient of performance best be optimized and how can the DH area
best be minimized when the variables in the HEX are varied?
In the following, short problem questions are listed and by answering these it may
help deﬁning the problem statement of the thesis:
• Is the shell and plate heat exchanger a better solution to use than the plate heat
exchanger?
• By changing the HEX type applied for the DH conﬁgurations, how much will the
COP increase?
• What inﬂuence does the HEX pressure drop have on the HP cycle of modeling?
• How does the choice of HEX aﬀect the total capital investment of the HP and DH
conﬁguration?
• Which HEX geometry variables and internal conditions have the greatest inﬂuence
on the COP and DH area?
• By varying the plate heat exchanger geometry and internal conditions, how much
can the COP be optimized and DH area be minimized?
7
==PAGE:23==
1.3
Task and Methods
In order to follow the time schedule of the thesis, the work has been divided into seven
tasks:
1. The ﬁrst task of the thesis is to perform a literature study regarding how large-scale
ammonia HPs works and how they can be combined with DH. The study will look
into how HP components can thermodynamically be modelled in the commercial
software package Engineering Equation Solver (EES). A further literature study will
investigate which correlation factors should be used for calculating the heat transfer
coeﬃcients and pressure drops in the evaporator, condensers and desuperheaters.
2. The second task is to validate the heat exchanger EES codes with the chosen heat
transfer correlation for PHEX and SPHEX against result from real manufacturers.
A comparison between the calculated EES result and manufacturer result will be
performed. The comparison will focus on the heat transfer area and pressure loss
etc.
3. The third task is to build the simple DH conﬁguration in EES. Here condenser units
for the lower and upper cycle will be connected in series. The found heat transfer
correlations and pressure loss correlations will be applied to the thermodynamic
model. Simulations will be performed for the two HEX types: PHEX and SPHEX.
4. Task four is to increase the complexity of the DH conﬁguration by adding a desu-
perheater after compressor 1 and 3, respectively. Simulations with the two HEX
types will again be performed.
5. The ﬁfth task is to compare the results produced from the four thermodynamic EES
models of the DH conﬁguration. The comparison will look at how the COP, overall
heat transfer coeﬃcients and pressure drop will change in the simulations.
6. The sixth task is to economically evaluate the best thermodynamically performing
DH conﬁgurations for the SPHEX and PHEX. The economical evaluation will cal-
culate the total purchase equipment cost, ﬁxed capital investment and total capital
investment for the two conﬁgurations.
7. The seventh task it to perform a sensitivity analysis of the best performing DH
conﬁguration from the economic evaluation. The sensitivity analysis will investigate
how the COP, total DH area and total pump work change when the HEX geometry
and internal conditions change. The variables having the greatest inﬂuence on the
COP in the sensitivity analysis will be used as independent variables for optimizing
of the COP and minimizing of the DH area.
8
==PAGE:24==
1.4
Reader’s Guide
The thesis is structured according to the classical scientiﬁc paper format. It comprises 5
chapters in total. The ﬁve chapters contain:
Chapter 1 - Introduction: the introduction section introduces the background and
motivation, problem statement and problem questions, tasks and methods and provides
a quick introduction to how the HP and its components work.
Chapter 2 - Methods: the method section explains the HP conﬁguration of Design
1 and Design 2, how the HPs have been thermodynamically modelled and dimensioned,
how the heat exchangers have been validated, how the economic analysis have been used
to compare the DH conﬁgurations and ﬁnally, how the sensitivity analysis has been used
to optimize the optimal DH conﬁguration.
Chapter 3 - Results: the result section provides the results for the validation of the
HEX components, the comparison of the DH conﬁgurations, the results obtained from the
economic analysis, the results from the sensitivity analysis and ﬁnally, the results from
the COP and DH area optimization.
Chapter 4 - Discussion: the discussion section discusses the methods used and the
results presented in the result section.
Chapter 5 - Conclusion: the conclusion answers the problem statement and prob-
lem questions of the thesis.

==PAGE:25==
1.5
The Heat Pump
Before starting on the method section and getting into how the large-scale HP and DH
conﬁgurations have been mathematically modelled in EES, some fundamental knowledge
regarding the HP will be explained.
1.5.1
Principle of the HP
The general purpose of the HP is to extract heat from a low temperature heat source
and reject heat to a high temperature heat sink. The process must follow the guidelines
of the second law of thermodynamics. The second law determines that it is impossible
for any cycle to produce heat by letting energy go from a cold medium towards a hot
medium without transferring any work to the system. So, when ejecting heat Q2 to a
high temperature sink, it is the sum of the heat Q1 extracted from a low temperature heat
source plus the work E added to the HP cycle, see Figure (1.6). In other words, E is the
work required to operate the cycle, and without the work, the HP cycle will contradict
the second law of thermodynamics [7].
Figure 1.6: Working principle of the heat pump.
10
==PAGE:26==
1.5.2
The Reversed Carnot HP
The reversed Carnot cycle is the most eﬃcient HP cycle. The cycle operates in an anti-
clock direction between a low and a high temperature level, see Figure (1.7).
Figure 1.7: The Carnot cycle in a TS-diagram. The numbers indicate the thermodynamic
state points.
During the cycle operation, the ﬂuid undergoes four reversible processes [7]:
1 →2:
A reversible isentropic compression of the ﬂuid from Tlow to Thigh
without any heat transferred to the surrounding.
2 →3:
A reversible isothermal compression at Thigh while the heat Q2
is being transferred from the refrigerant to the heat sink.
3 →4:
A reversible isentropic expansion of the ﬂuid from from Thigh to Tlow
without any heat transfer to the surroundings.
4 →1:
A reversible isothermal expansion at Tlow while the heat Q1
is being transferred to the working ﬂuid from the heat source.
Even though the reverse Carnot cycle is the most eﬀective HP cycle, it cannot be fully
imitated for a real HP cycle. The reason is that the isentropic expansion and compression
in fact are irreversible. Due to initial and maintenance costs, the machinery is used for
the isentropic expansion between 3 and 4 replaced by a simple expansion device which
throttles the refrigerant isenthalpically from a high to a low pressure. During this process,
work that could be recovered is wasted instead. Moreover, the isentropic compression
device between state 1 and 2 cannot tolerate a liquid phase in the machinery. This means
that the isentropic compression process must be taken out of the two-phase zone. The
11
==PAGE:27==
deviation from the reversed Carnot cycle creates irritability which decreases the COP of
the HP due to the fact that more power is needed [8].
1.5.3
The Simple Vapor Compression Cycle
The simple vapor compression refrigerant cycle is the most common cycle used for HP.
The cycle has four main components: an evaporator, a compressor, a condenser and an
expansion device, see Figure (1.8).
Figure 1.8: PH-log diagram of a simple vapor compression cycle. The colours represents
the temperature levels of the working refrigerant with red for hot and blue for cold [3].
The working refrigerant of the HP is ﬂowing in an anti-clock direction through the
four thermodynamic state points. At point 1, the refrigerant has just left the evaporator
and is in a superheated vapor form. From point 1 to 2, the refrigerant goes through the
compressor. The compressor increases the temperature, pressure and enthalpy of the ﬂuid
by transferring work to the ﬂuid. At stage 2, the superheated, high-pressure refrigerant
enters the condenser unit. In the condenser unit, energy is being transferred from the hot
refrigerant ﬂuid to a heat sink media. The condenser unit can be divided into three zones;
a desuperheater, a condensation and a subcooler zone. In the desuperheater zone, the
temperature and enthalpy of the refrigerant decreases until the refrigerant phase appears
in a saturated vapor form. In the condensation zone, the refrigerant condensates from
saturated vapor to saturated liquid. In this process, the temperature is being constant
12
==PAGE:28==
and the enthalpy is decreasing. In the subcooler zone, the temperature and the enthalpy
decrease while the ﬂuid goes from a saturated liquid into the wet domain. At point 3, the
ﬂuid leaves the condenser unit. From state point 3 to 4, the refrigerant ﬂows through the
expansion device where the pressure, temperature is being decreased while the enthalpy
is constant. At stage 4, the refrigerant enters the evaporator unit. In the evaporator unit,
energy is being transferred from the low temperature heat source to the refrigerant ﬂuid.
The evaporator unit can be divided up into two zones: an evaporator and a superheater
zone. In the evaporator zone, the temperature of the refrigerant is constant while the
enthalpy increases until the phase becomes saturated vapor. In the superheater zone, the
temperature starts increasing while the enthalpy increases furthermore. The refrigerant
leaves the evaporator at state point 1 and the cycles continue all over again.
The subcooling and superheating also work as precaution for the cycle’s equipment.
The extra heat removed in the subcooler ensures that no gas bubbles enters the throttling
device and creates shock waves.
The extra heat transferred to the refrigerant in the
superheater ensures that no liquid droplets goes into the compressor [3].
The condenser unit can be designed as a single condenser unit containing the desuper-
heater, condenser and subcooler zone alone or as three HEXs each with their own zone.
The same applies to the evaporator which can be designed as a single unit with an evapo-
ration and superheating zone or as two individual HEXs each with their own zone. In the
SVAF HP, the two condenser units are split up into a set of a desuperheater, condenser
and subcooler. By giving each zone its own HEX, it is much easier to control when the
phase transition between the ﬂuid phases takes place. However, it requires receivers to
do so. Moreover, any liquid or vapor is also avoided into the wrong condenser zone.
13
==PAGE:29==
1.5.4
The Heat Exchanger
A heat exchanger is a device used to transfer heat between two moving ﬂuids streams
without mixing them. The heat exchangers are widely used in various industries and
they are available in variable sizes and designs. Depending on the HEX’s material and
thermodynamic limitations, it can be used as a condenser, an evaporator or even as an
internal heat exchanger. As mentioned in section (1.1), plate heat exchangers and shell
and plate heat exchanger are the two HEX types of study in this thesis.
The Plate Heat Exchanger
The plate heat exchanger (PHEX) is probably one of the most applied HEX types when
it comes to industrial applications as refrigeration, heating or cooling. In Figure (1.9) a
semi welded gasket PHEX from Alfa Laval is presented.
Figure 1.9: Semi welded gasket plate heat exchanger from Alfa Laval [9]
On the Figure it can be seen that the PHEX has a square and compact design. The
compact design gives the PHEX a large heat transfer area per unit volume.
This is
an advantage when the space is limited or the PHEX has to be installed on expensive
property. The compact design also means that the PHEX requires a less refrigerant charge
and has a lighter structural support compared to other HEX types. The square plates
of the PHEX is typically made of stainless steel or titanium depending on the working
refrigerant. Between each plate gaskets are placed. On the plates itself, a corrugated wavy
pattern is stamped. The wavy pattern increases the plate heat surface area by 10-25%
compared to an ordinary ﬂat plate HEX. When the plates are stacked together, the wavy
pattern forms small hydraulic channels for the ﬂuids, which control the ﬂuid motion and
14
==PAGE:30==
enhance the heat transfer from the hot to the cold ﬂuid media. The PHEX is relatively
easy to clean because the plates can be taken on and oﬀ. Hereby fouling can be prevented,
and undesired material on the plates can be washed away. Moreover, it is easy to change
the heat load of the PHEX by simply adding or removing plates [10].
The Shell and Plate Heat Exchanger
The shell and plate heat exchanger, SPHEX, is a compromise between a shell and tube
HEX and a PHEX. On Figure (1.10a) and (1.10b) a Vahterus SPHEX and a Figure
showing the working principle of a PHEX are presented.
(a)
(b)
Figure 1.10: Figure a: Vahterus SPHEX. Fig b: working principle of a Vahterus SPHEX.
The red arrows indicate the hot ﬂuid and the blue arrows indicate the cold ﬂuid [11]
As is can be seen on Figure (1.10b), the SPHEX shell consists of a shell cylinder which
is closed oﬀby a single O-ring and a shell ﬂange. Inside the cylinder, the circular plates
are placed. The plates are welded together so it consists of a single gasket-free plate pack.
The plate pack is isolated so it will not touch the shell side. By using plates instead of
tubes, the SPHEX can obtain a higher thermal performance per unit volume than the
shell and tube HEX. As the PHEX, the SPHEX is also easy to clean in order to prevent
fouling. Moreover, the geometry of the plates can be changed by adding a new plate pack
with more or less plates. However, as the plate pack is placed inside a shell, it cannot
handle as much plates as in a PHEX. The SPHEX has a higher resistance against thermal
fatigue than PHEX, because the plate pack is not welded along four corners sides as the
pure welded PHEX [10].
15
==PAGE:31==
1.5.5
The Compressor
The purpose of a compressor is to transfer the vapor from a low-pressure evaporator to a
high-pressure condenser. The compressor can be divided into two main groups; positive
displacement compressors and dynamic compressors. The positive displacement compres-
sors group can further be divided into two subgroups which are reciprocating compressors,
also called piston compressors, and rotary compressors. A reciprocating compressor can,
for example, be a single acting compressor and a double acting compressor.
The ro-
tary compressor can, for example, be a scroll compressor, screw compressors and a vane
compressor [12].
The positive displacement compressor works by gas which is trapped in a space. The
volume of the space is reduced when the axis which drives the compressor is rotated. As
the volume is reduced, the gas will increase its pressure. The gas is discharged to the
high-pressure side in portions. The dynamic compressor works by the gas, due to the
fact that it is given a high speed by the compressor impeller. Before the gas leaves the
compressor, it is going through a defuser where the pressure increases further, and the
gas velocity is reduced [12].
In the positive displacement compressor, valves are used to control the gas ﬂow. The
valves are among the most sensitive parts of the compressor, and they often settle the life
expectancy and eﬃciency of the compressor. In the compressor, the valves prevent the
compressor from rotating backward when it is stopped. A valve compressor can also work
as an expansion machine and extract work from an expanding gas [12].
In the thesis, piston compressors are chosen for the large-scale ammonia HP. The
reason why piston compressors are chosen is that they have a large working domain.
Moreover, the piston compressors do not require oil separation and oil cooling as screw
compressors do. In Figure (1.11) a semihermetic compressor is presented.
Figure 1.11: A cross section of a semihermetic compressor from GEA [13]. The blue
arrows indicate the refrigerant vapor path through the compressor.
16
==PAGE:32==
In a semihermetic compressor, the electric motor is built inside the compressor enclo-
sure. As the semihermetic compressor has a bolted end ﬂange, is it possible to dismantle
it. As the motor is placed inside the enclosed compressor, the motor windings must be
cooled down. Often the windings are cooled down by the incoming refrigerant vapor. By
letting the refrigerant vapor pass through the motor winding, an extra superheat before
compression is obtained [12].
17
==PAGE:33==
Chapter 2
Methods
In the method section, the theory behind the thesis will be presented and explained.
Initially, it will be explained how the conﬁgurations of Design 1 and Design 2 work.
Afterwards it will be explained how the cycle conditions have been determined and how
the HP heat load has been distributed between the HEXs. Then follows a description how
the COP has been determined for DH conﬁgurations. Subsequently, an explanation how
the components have been geometrically and thermodynamically modelled in EES will
follow. Now the theory behind the HEX validation and economic evaluation of the best DH
conﬁguration will be presented and explained. And ﬁnally, the method of the sensitivity
analysis used to optimize the COP of the best DH conﬁguration will be presented.
2.1
The Conﬁguration of Design 1 and 2
This method section is dedicated for presenting and explaining the conﬁgurations of De-
sign 1 and Design 2. The two designs are both a 5 MW large scale ammonia HP which
utilizes sea water as heat source and produces district heating for the DH grid at Sjæl-
landsbroen. In Figure (2.1) and Figure (2.2) the conﬁguration of Design 1 and 2 can be
seen. Design 1 and Design 2 both consist of two HP units. Each HP unit is operating at
a low and high pressure stage. The individual HP units consist of two piston compressors
connected in series over an open ﬂash intercooler (IC). The evaporator used is a ﬂooded
HEX connected to a separator. In the beginning of the sea water pipes and DH pipe,
centrifugal pumps are mounted. The function of these pumps is to increase the inlet
pressure of the ﬂuids so pressure losses in the HEX’s can be overcome. By having these
pumps, it is also ensured that the right inlet pressure is always delivered to the system.
The major diﬀerence between the two conﬁgurations is that Design 2 has a desuper-
heater after compressor 1 and 3 (DSHL and DSHH). By having a desuperheater here,
the overheated refrigerant is cooled down before it enters the open IC. The DH water in
the DH network in Design 2 ﬂows ﬁrst through the low pressure DSHL and DSHH before
it enters the condenser unit (SC, CON and DSH). Hereby the maximum allowable heat
transfer from the refrigerant to the DH water in the two desuperheaters is obtained.
As both DH conﬁgurations consist of two similar HP units, only the refrigerant cycle
of the lower HP will be explained. At state point 1, the ammonia leaves the separator as
saturated vapor and enters compressor 1. In compressor 1, work (W1) is transferred to the
18
==PAGE:34==
ammonia and the pressure and temperature of the refrigerant increases. For Design 1, the
superheated refrigerant enters directly into an open ﬂash intercooler after compressor 1.
For Design 2, the superheated refrigerant vapor ﬂows into desuperheater (DSHL) where
it is cooled down before it enters the open ﬂash intercooler. At state point 3, saturated
ammonia leaves the open ﬂash intercooler and enters into compressor 2.
Compressor
2 transfers work (W2) to the refrigerant and the ammonia temperature and pressures
increases even further. At state point 4, the hot ammonia refrigerant leaves compressor
2 and enters into condenser unit 1. In condenser unit 1, the refrigerant ﬂows through
a desuperheater zone, a condenser zone, and a subcooling zone. In each zone, heat is
transferred from the refrigerant to the water in the DH network. The refrigerant leaves
the condenser unit at point 7 where it is throttled through a valve which decreases the
pressure. The refrigerant reenters the open ﬂash intercooler at state point 8. At state
point 9, at the bottom of the open ﬂash intercooler, the refrigerant leaves as a saturated
liquid. The refrigerant ﬂows once more through a valve and the pressure reduces further
before the refrigerant enters the separator at state point 10. At the bottom of the separator
at state point 11, saturated liquid leaves the tank and ﬂows into the evaporator. In the
evaporator, the ammonia receives energy from the sea water. The refrigerant leaves the
evaporator at state point 12 and reenters the separator once more and the cycle repeats
itself. The upper cycle works in the same way.
19
==PAGE:35==
Figure 2.1: PI-diagram of Design 1. The black pipeline symbolizes the sea water, the red
pipeline symbolizes the R717 and the blue pipeline symbolizes the DH water. Condenser
unit 1 and condenser unit 2 are arranged so they are parallel.
20
==PAGE:36==
Figure 2.2: PI-diagram of Design 2. The black pipeline symbolizes the sea water, the red
pipeline symbolizes the R717 and the blue pipeline symbolized the DH water. The DH
water ﬂows through the HEX in the following order; DSHL, condenser unit 1, DSHH and
condenser unit 2 before it is returns to the DH network.

2.1.2
Load Distribution
In the EES models, the 5 MW heat load is given as the input variable ˙Qtot. The heat
load is distributed equally 50-50% between HP 1 and HP 2. By knowing the heat load
distribution, the overall energy Eq. (2.3a) and Eq. (2.3b) for Design 1 can be established.
˙Qtot/2 = ˙QSC1 + ˙QCON1 + ˙QDSH1
(2.3a)
˙Qtot/2 = ˙QSC2 + ˙QCON2 + ˙QDSH2
(2.3b)
For Design 2, the two desuperheaters DSHL and DSHH should also be included. The
two energy equations then become
˙Qtot/2 = ˙QSC1 + ˙QCON1 + ˙QDSH1 + ˙QDSHL
(2.4a)
˙Qtot/2 = ˙QSC2 + ˙QCON2 + ˙QDSH2 + ˙QDSHH

2.1.3
Cycle Eﬃciency
The coeﬃcient of performance (COP) is a variable used to evaluate the eﬃciency of a
refrigeration or HP cycle. In an HP, the COP is the ratio between the heat load capacity
˙Qtot and the total power Wtot delivered to the system.
In other words, COP can be
thought of as [8].
COP = ”what you get”
”what you pay”
⇒
COP =
˙Qtot
˙Wtot
(2.5)
The higher the COP value, the better is the eﬃciency of the cycle. In the EES-model,
the 5 MW heat load is the ˙Qtot we get transferred to the DH grid. The power we pay
˙Wtot is the sum of the compressor and pump power. The COP of Design 1 and 2 can be
expressed by Eq. (3.3).
COP =
˙Qtot
˙Wtot
⇒
COP =
˙Qtot

k=1
˙Wcomp,k + Pkpump
k=1
˙Wpump,k
(2.6)
where k is the number of compressor and pump components, respectively. The the-
oretical limit of the COP for the HP is the Carnot COP. From the Reverse Carnot HP
(1.5.2) section, the Carnot COP can be expressed as
COPCarnot =
Thot
Thot −Tcold
(2.7)
By dividing the COP from the HP with the Carnot COP, the Carnot eﬃciency ηcarnot can
be obtained, see Eq. (2.8) [14].
ηCarnot =
COP

(2.8)
The Carnot eﬃciency tells how close the real HP is to the ideal COP. The eﬃciency
normally lies between 50% to 70% [15].

2.2
System Modelling
This section is dedicated to the geometry dimension and thermodynamic modelling of the
diﬀerent components used in the HP cycle.
2.2.1
Compressor
The function of the compressor is to increase the pressure of the working refrigerant.
When the ﬂuid leaves the compressor, the temperature is above the sink media temper-
ature and the ﬂuid can hereby transfer its energy to the sink media inside the condenser
unit. The section will use compressor 1 as a reference component for the equations. The
equations presented are applicable to all the compressors in Design 1 and 2. In the mod-
elling of the compressor, the following assumptions are made.
Assumptions:
• Steady state process.
• No heat loss (adiabatic process).
• Negligible kinetic and potential energy.
The compressor is treated as the control volume (CV) boundary. The work from the
compressor to the refrigerant can be derived from the energy equation, see Eq. (2.9).
dU

By applying the

kinetic and speciﬁc potential energy changes across the compressor disappear, see Eq.
(2.10).

real compression. The outlet speciﬁc enthalpy for an ideal compression h2s is calculated

simulation, a value of 0,7 is used according to [8].

2.2.2
Expansion Valve
The function of the expansion valve is to expand the refrigerant, so the pressure decreases.
In the HP cycle, the expansion valve also controls the level of refrigerant in the separator
and open ﬂash intercooler. As reference component for the equations, valve 1 from HP 1
will be used. The equations presented are applicable to all the expansion valves in Design
1 and 2. Following assumptions are made in order to model the valve.
Assumptions:
• Steady state process.
• No heat loss (adiabatic process).
• No work transferred.
• Negligible kinetic and potential energy.
The expansion valve is treated as the CV boundary. The speciﬁc enthalpy change over
the valve can be derived from the energy equation, see Eq. (2.14).

2.2.3
Pump
The purpose of a pump is the same as of a compressor, to increase the pressure of a ﬂuid.
As reference component, the DH pump will be used for the equations. The equation
presented here is applicable for all pumps in Design 1 and 2. Following assumptions are
made in order to model the pump.
Assumptions:
• Steady state process.
• No heat loss (adiabatic process).
• Negligible kinetic and potential energy.
The inlet and outlet of the pump are treated as the CV boundary. The work from
the pump to the refrigerant can be derived from Bernoulli’s extended equation, see Eq.
(2.18).
−˙W5 = ˙V (PDH2 −PDH1) + 1

and speciﬁc potential energy changes across the pump disappear, see Eq. (2.19).
−˙W5 = ˙V (PDH2 −PDH1)
(2.19)

PDH2 = PDH1 + ∆Ptot,sink
(2.21)

2.2.4
Separator and Intercooler
The function of the separator is to collect the refrigerant leaving the ﬂooded evaporator.
As the outlet quality of the evaporator is only 0,7, the purpose of separator is to sepa-
rate the ﬂuid phases, so the compressor does not receive any liquid droplets. The open
ﬂash intercooler function it to cool down the refrigerant so the next compressor work is
reduced. The intercooler receives refrigerant from the lower stage compressor and high
pressure condenser unit. In this section, separator 1 and intercooler 1 from HP 1 will be
used as reference for the equations. Following assumptions are made for the separator
and intercooler in order to model them in EES.
Assumptions:
• Steady state process.
• No heat loss through walls (adiabatic).
• Negligible kinetic and potential energy.
• No work interactions.
The inlets and outlets of the separator and intercooler are treated as the CV boundary.
A common energy equation for the separator and intercooler can be derived from Eq.
(2.23).

(2.24)

Refrigeration Charge and Dimension of the Separator and Intercooler
The working refrigerant charge of the HP is based on the size of the evaporators, con-
densers and desuperheaters. The working charge m of an individual HEX is estimated by
calculating the volume occupied by the refrigerant ﬂuid multiplied by the mean speciﬁc
volume 1/¯v of the ﬂuid, see Eq. (2.27) .
mk = Mk · Wk · Lk · bk · 1
¯vk
(2.27)
Here L is the plate length, W is the plate width, b is the plate press depth, M is
the No. of refrigerant channels and k is the component number. The total refrigerant
charge mtot of the system is the sum of the working refrigerant charge in each individual
HEX component. For Design 1, the charge contributes are: evaporator 1, evaporator 2,
condenser 1 unit, condenser 2 unit. For Design 2, the charge contributes are: evaporator
1, evaporator 2, condenser 1 unit, condenser 2 unit, DSHL and DSHH.
The low stage separator 1 and 2 are designed in such a way that they can contain the
refrigerant charge of the nearby evaporator and desuperheater. The separator volume is
over-sized by 25% as suggested by [19]. The separator volumes V for HP 1 and HP 2
are calculated by Eq. (2.28a) and (2.28b). The over-size separators ensured a saturated
liquid state at the outlet of the separator at stage point 11 and 23.
Vseparator1 = (mevap1 + mDSHL) · ¯v · 1, 25
(2.28a)
Vseparator2 = (mevap2 + mDSHH) · ¯v · 1, 25
(2.28b)
Here mevap1, mDSHL, mevap2 and mDSHH are the working refrigerant charge in; evaporator
1, desuperheater (DSHL), evaporator 2 and desuperheater (DSHH). The two intercoolers
are designed in such a way that they can contain the refrigerant charge from condenser 1
unit and condenser 2 unit, respectively. Their volumes are also over-sized by 25%. The
intercooler volumes V for HP 1 and HP 2 are calculated by Eq. (2.29a) and (2.29b). The
over-sizing of the two intercoolers ensures a saturated liquid state at the outlet of the
intercooler at state point 9 and 21.
Vintercooler1 = mcond1 · ¯v · 1, 25
(2.29a)
Vintercooler2 = mcond2 · ¯v · 1, 25
(2.29b)
where mcond1 and mcond2 are the working refrigerant charge in condenser unit 1 and
condenser unit 2.

==PAGE:46==
Range of the Plate Geometry
When modelling the plate geometry in EES, it is important that the plate has realistic
dimensions. In order to have realistic dimensions, the plate geometry must be within
some speciﬁc geometry ranges.
Plate Geometry Ranges:
• The wave length must be between Λ ≃5-7 mm [22].
• The ratio between the wave-length Λ and the plate press depth b must be within
1-4 [22].
• The ratio between the length and width L/W for PHEX must be between 1-4 [22].
For modelling the plate geometry in EES, Λ has been given the value 6 mm and the
plate press depth b the value of 2 mm. The ratio Λ/b is hereby equal to 3 which is within
the allowable geometry range. The ratio between the length and width L/W has been
given the value 1 in the EES code. The ratio L/W = 1 is not the most optimal ratio, but
the EES code converge in a better way for this setting.
Mass Flux of the HEX Channels
Inside the PHEX and SPHEX channels, the working ﬂuids is ﬂowing. The mass ﬂux
for the refrigerant and water in a PHEX is calculated by Eq. (2.35) and Eq. (2.36),
respectively.
Gref =

(2.35)

(2.36)
where ˙mref and ˙mwater are the mass ﬂow of refrigerant and water going into the HEX,
ntot is the total number of HEX plates. For SPHEX the width W in Eq. (2.35) and Eq.
(2.36) is substituted by the plate diameter Dp.

Number of HEX Channel
In order to determine the prices of the separator and intercooler in Design 1 and Design
2, the size of the HEX must be calculated. The HEX size is estimated from the number of
channels in the unit. In a HEX, the number of refrigerant channels Mref can be calculated
by Eq. (2.37).
2ΦMref = Atot
A0
(2.37)
where Φ is plate enlargement factor, Atot is the total heat transfer area of the HEX
unit and A0 is projected plate surface area. In Figure (2.5) is presented a cross section of
a condenser unit containing 6 plates and 5 channels.
Figure 2.5: Cross section of a condenser unit containing 6 plates and 5 ﬂuid channels.
From Figure (2.5) it can be seen that the total number of water channels Mwater is
equal to the total number of HEX plates ntot divided by two, see Eq. (2.38).
Mwater = ntot
2
(2.38)
Moreover, can it be seen that there is one more water channel than refrigerant channel.
The total number of refrigerant channels can hereby be calculated with Eq. (2.39).
Mref = Mwater −1
(2.39)
If Mwater is chosen instead of Mref in Eq. (2.37), it will result in a smaller plate surface
projection area A0 which will result in over-dimensioning of the plate numbers.
32
==PAGE:48==
Channel velocity of the HEX
When applying a HEX, it is important to control the number of plates. If the No. of
plates decreases, the Reynolds No. increases as a result of a higher mass ﬂux passing
through the HEX channels. A higher Reynolds No. leads to a more turbulent ﬂuid that
has a higher heat transfer coeﬃcient. A higher heat transfer coeﬃcient means that less
area is needed for the heat transfer. However, there are limitations with regards to the
increase of the heat transfer coeﬃcient. This means, when the No. of plates decreases, the
length of the remaining plates must increase as a result. The extra plate length gives a
higher frictional pressure drop of the ﬂuid. To overcome this pressure loss, the compressors
must provide a higher work input to the cycle which causes a less COP value. If, on the
other hand, the No. of plates increases instead, the pressure loss will decrease because
of shorter plate lengths and the COP will grow. However, the HEX cannot contain an
inﬁnity No. of plates. Additionally, the more plates used in the HP, the more expensive
it gets. Therefore is it necessary to ﬁnd a compromise between the No. of plates used
and the COP of the HP.
In the thesis, the No. of plates is controlled by the HEX channel velocity of the water.
From [22] it is stated that the water channel velocity should lie between 0,2 m/s to 0,8
m/s. In the EES code, the HEX channel velocity of the water has been given the value
of 0,25 m/s. By applying the velocity to Eq. (2.40), the cross-section of an HEX can be
calculated.
Across =
˙mwater
˙V · ρwater,in
(2.40)
where ˙mwater is the mass ﬂow of water, ˙V is the volumetric ﬂow of water and ρwater,in is
the water inlet density. By substituting Across into Eq. (2.41), the total number of water
channels Mwater can be estimated.
Mwater = Across
b · W
(2.41)
For SPHEX, the width W is substituted by the diameter Dp. By applying Eq. (2.37)
to Eq. (2.41) and setting the length and width ratio L/W equal to 1 for PHEX, the
total number of HEX plates can be derived. Moreover, the length Lp and width W in
PHEX and the diameter Dp in PHEX become independent variables. This means that
the DH conﬁguration of PHEX and SPHEX can be compared without applying speciﬁc
HEX dimensions to the EES code.

==PAGE:49==
2.2.6
Condenser
The condenser is one of the most important components in the HP. The function of the
condenser is to transfer heat from the working refrigerant to the sink media.
In this
section, the condenser unit 1 form Design 1 will be used as a reference for the equations.
The equations presented here are applicable for the other condenser units in Design 1 and
2. Following assumptions are made in order to model the condenser unit in EES.
Assumptions:
• Steady state process.
• No heat loss through walls (adiabatic).
• Negligible kinetic and potential energy.
• There is no work interactions.
As mentioned in the introduction, the condenser unit can be divided into three zones:
desuperheater, condenser and subcooler see Figure (2.6).
Figure 2.6: TQ-diagram of a counter ﬂow condenser divided into three zones: desuper-
heater, condenser and subcooler. The red arrow symbolizes the hot refrigerant and the
blue arrow symbolizes the cold sink media.
The temperatures of the three zones are calculated from the input refrigerant temper-
ature T4, input sink media temperature TDH2 and an input pinch temperature diﬀerence
∆Tpinch. The temperature of the condenser zone is deﬁned by Eq. (2.42).
Tref,cond = TDH4 + ∆Tpinch
(2.42)
34
==PAGE:50==
The outlet temperature of the refrigerant T7 is given by Eq. (2.43).
T7 = TDH2 + ∆Tpinch
(2.43)
The delta pinch temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch is the factor which determines how
close the sink media temperature comes to the refrigerant temperature. The delta pinch
temperature diﬀerence is hereby the factor which decides how large the heat transfer area
must be in a condenser in order to transfer the needed heat load ˙Q to the sink media.
As a general rule of thumb, the smaller the delta pinch temperature diﬀerence, the more
expensive the condenser unit becomes. The heat load of each refrigerant zone can be
expressed by Eq. (2.44).
˙Qi = Ui · Ai · LMTDi
(2.44)
Here ˙Q is the heat transferred in each zone, U is the overall heat transferred coeﬃcient,
A is the heat transfer area, LMTD is the Logarithmic mean temperature diﬀerence and
i indicates the speciﬁc condenser zone. The LMTD is calculated by Eq. (2.45).
LMTDi = ∆Tin −∆Tout
ln

∆Tin
∆Tout

(2.45)
Here ∆Tin and ∆Tout are the temperature diﬀerences between the hot and cold ﬂuid
at the inlet and outlet of the HEX zones. The calculation of the temperature diﬀerence
depends whether the ﬂow arrangement is co-current or counter-current, see Figure (2.7)
[23].
(a)
(b)
Figure 2.7: Fig a: the temperature along the HEX length for co-current ﬂow. Fig b: the
temperature along the HEX length for counter-current ﬂow. The arrow heads indicate
the ﬂow direction and the colours red and blue symbolize the hot ﬂuid and cold ﬂuid,
respectively.
35
==PAGE:51==
In a condenser unit, the counter-current ﬂow is often most desirable. This is due to
the fact that the counter-current ﬂow has a more uniform temperature diﬀerence between
the hot and cold ﬂuid. The more uniform temperature diﬀerence minimizes the thermal
stresses along the HEX length and produces a better heat transfer through the HEX.
In the thesis, the counter-current conﬁguration is used for all the condenser units and
desuperheaters (DSHL and DSHH). For a co-current ﬂow arrangement, the temperature
diﬀerences are calculated by Eq. (2.46a) and (2.46b).
∆Tin = Thot,in −Tcold,in
(2.46a)
∆Tout = Thot,out −Tcold,out
(2.46b)
For a counter-current ﬂow arrangement, the temperature diﬀerences are calculated by
Eq. (2.47a) and (2.47b).
∆Tin = Thot,in −Tcold,out
(2.47a)
∆Tout = Thot,out −Tcold,in
(2.47b)

calculated by equation (2.48).

coeﬃcient for the refrigerant αref and sink media αwater is given by the Nusselt No, see
Eq. (2.49).

2.2.7
Evaporator
The evaporator is one of the main components of the HP cycle. In an HP, the function of
the evaporator is to transfer energy from a low temperature heat source to the refrigerant.
In this section, evaporator 1 is used as reference unit for the equations. The equations
presented here are applicable for the other evaporators in Design 1 and Design 2. The
assumptions for the evaporator is the same as in the condenser unit. In Figure (2.8) a
TQ-diagram of evaporator 1 with a co-current ﬂow is presented. The reason why a co-
current ﬂow arrangement is used for the ﬂooded evaporator is that the large temperature
diﬀerence in the beginning of the HEX ∆T1, see Figure (2.7a) starts boiling the ﬂuid
earlier in the HEX [27].
Figure 2.8: TQ-diagram of a evaporator with co-current ﬂow. The red arrow indicates
the working refrigerant and the blue arrow indicates the source media. The arrow heads
indicate the ﬂow direction of the ﬂuid.
The evaporating temperature of the refrigerant R717 is calculated by the two temper-
ature inputs; sea source outlet temperature Tsea2 and the pinch temperature diﬀerence
∆Tpinch, see Figure (2.52).
Tref,evap = Tsea2 −∆Tpinch
(2.52)
The heat transferred from the source media to the refrigerant is calculated by Eq.
(2.44), where the overall heat transfer coeﬃcient U is calculated by Eq.
(2.48) and
LMTD is calculated from Eq.
(2.45).
Finally, the heat transfer coeﬃcients for the
refrigerant and heat source media water are calculated by the Nusselt No. (2.49) and
imperial correlations. In Table (2.3) the used correlations for PHEX and SPHEX are
presented.

2.2.9
Pressure Drop in Heat Exchanger
In order to simulate plausible condenser unit, evaporator and desuperheater in EES,
the pressure drop must be included. The pressure drop consists of four pressure drop
contributions: a frictional pressure drop ∆Pfri created by the channels, a gravity pressure
drop ∆Pg, an acceleration/deceleration pressure drop ∆Pacc and a pressure drop from the
inlet and outlet ports ∆Pp. By summing up these four pressure drop contributions for
each single HEX zone, the overall pressure drop for each HEX side can be calculated, see
Eq. (2.54) [10].
∆Ptotal = ∆Pfri + ∆Pg + ∆Pacc + ∆Pp
(2.54)
For a homogeneous and steady ﬂuid, the port pressure drop ∆Pp is calculated by Eq.
(2.55).
∆Pp = 0.75M
G2
p
2ρ

in
+
G2
p
2ρ

out

(2.55)
Here ρin and ρout are the densities deﬁned by the ﬂuid states at the inlet and outlet
of the ports, M is the total number of channels for the respective ﬂuid and G is the
mass ﬂux. The port pressure loss can easily be over-estimated because the condenser
unit is seen as a single unit having a desuperheater, a condenser and a subcooler zone.
In order to avoid this, the port pressure drop is only calculated for the ﬁrst zone that
the refrigerant and water enters. In the desuperheater HEX and evaporator, the port
pressure drop is calculated normally because there is only one zone considered.
The
acceleration/deceleration pressure drop term for a multi-phase homogeneous and steady
ﬂuid is given by Eq. (2.56).
∆Pacc = G2∆x
 1
ρv
−1
ρl

(2.56)
Here ∆x is the quality diﬀerence between saturated vapor and saturated liquid. For a
single phase zone ∆x takes the value 1 and the two densities ρv and ρl are substitutes by
the input ρin and output ρout densities for the considered zone, Eq (2.56) then becomes
∆Pacc = G2
 1

(2.57)
The elevation pressure drop for a multi-phase and single-phase ﬂuid zone is calculated
by Eq. (2.58).
∆Pg = ρmgLi
(2.58)
Here ρm is the mean density for the zone, g is the gravity constant and Li is the plate
length of the zone. Finally, the frictional pressure drop is given by Eq. (2.59)[20].
∆Pfri = 2fLiG2

(2.59)

Length of the Condenser Zones
In order not to over-estimate the pressure drop of the condenser unit, the desuperheater
length ∆LDSH, condenser length ∆LCOND and subcooler length LSC must be derived so
it can be substituted into Li place in Eq. (2.59). In Figure (2.10) the three lengths are
presented for a condenser PHEX and SPHEX plate.
(a)

Figure b: a sketch of s SPHEX plate with the diameter Dp, desuperheater length ∆LDSH,
condenser length ∆Lcond and subcooling length ∆LSC presented.

Atot of the condenser unit, a length ratio for the speciﬁc zone can be calculated, see Eq.
(2.60a), Eq. (2.60b) and Eq. (2.60c).
Lratio,DSH = ADSH

By multiplying the individual length ratio with the total plate length L (L = LP for

Eq. (2.61a), Eq. (2.61b) and Eq. (2.61c).
∆LDSH = L · Lratio,DSH
(2.61a)
∆LCOND = L · Lratio,COND
(2.61b)
∆LSC = L · Lratio,SC
(2.61c)

L = ∆LDSH + ∆Lcond + ∆LSC

2.3
Heat Exchanger Validation
It can be tricky to develop a thermodynamic HEX code that produces the same result as
real HEX components. In order to determine how well the developed EES codes work, a
validation of the condenser and evaporator code will take place. The PHEX code will be
validated against data from a PHEX condenser and a PHEX evaporator from the Danish
manufacturer, Alfa Laval. The SPHEX will be validated against SPHEX data from a
SPHEX condenser and a SPHEX evaporator from the Finnish manufacturer, Vahterus.
The data sheets for the used PHEX and SPHEX are presented in Appendix (B). In order
to validate the HEX, following assumptions for the geometry and thermodynamic prop-
erties are made.
Assumptions:
• Plate press depth: b = 0,002 m
• Wave-length: Λ = 0, 006 m
• Plate corrugation angle: β = 30◦
• Thermal conductivity: k = 16 W/(mK)
In the condenser validation, a ”TK20BW” model from Alfa Laval is used for reference
for PHEX, and a ”PSHE 4HH-188/2/1” model from Vahterus is used for reference for
SPHEX. The TK20BW model has a length and a width of 1,525 m x 0,740 m. The
PSHE 4HH-188/2/1 has a diameter of Ø516. The heat load of the condenser is 810 kW.
Moreover will a fouling factor Rf of 0, 3553 · 10−4 be applied. The used ﬂuids are R717
and water. The input temperatures, pressures and mass ﬂow for each ﬂuid are presented
in Table (2.6).

==PAGE:62==
2.4
Economic Evaluation
In this section, the economic analysis used for evaluating the two best performing DH
conﬁgurations is presented.
The total capital investment (TCI) of an HP consists of
a direct, an indirect and an outlays costs.
The direct costs can be divided into two
subcategories; onsite and oﬀsite costs. The onsite costs cover the equipment used in the
HP cycle plus; installation, piping and control of the purchased equipment. The oﬀsite
costs concerns building land and civil architectural work of the HP plant. The indirect
costs cover the expenses concerning operation and maintenance (O&M). The outlays costs
cover the start up, working capital and research and development costs.
The estimation of the capital costs can be a comprehensive aﬀair. One reason for
that is that the manufacturers are often reluctant to inform the cost price of a speciﬁc
component. The manufacturer will provide the customer with a speciﬁc cost price in
each case rather than stating a general, uniform price. To accommodate this issue, the
purchase equipment cost (PEC) is here estimated through Eq. (2.63) [7].
CPEC,Y = CPEC,W
 XY
XW
γ
(2.63)
This equation calculates the PEC CPEC,Y for a speciﬁc dimension or size XY when
the cost price CPEC,W of a diﬀerent dimension or size XW is known. The exponent γ
is called the cost scaling exponent. The exponent is assumed to be constant within a
given unit or size range of the speciﬁc equipment. If γ is unknown, the exponent should
take the value of 0,6 according to the six-tenth rule [7]. In order to determine reason-
able PEC values for the components in the HP, the following assumptions have been made.
Assumptions:
• PEC for a PHEX/SPHEX condenser is a function of the heat transfer area and the
inlet pressure.
• PEC for a PHEX/SPHEX evaporator is a function of the heat transfer area and the
inlet pressure.
• PEC for a PHEX/SPHEX desuperheater is a function of the HEX area and the
inlet pressure.
• PEC for a centrifugal pump is a function of the work delivered from the pump to
the working refrigerant.
• PEC for a compressor is a function of the real compressor displacement volume and
the inlet pressure.
• PEC for a separator is a function of the volume occupied by the working refrigerant
in the evaporator and desuperheater.
• PEC for a open ﬂash intercooler is a function of the volume occupied by the working
refrigerant in the condenser unit.
47
==PAGE:63==
The estimated PEC for all the equipment must be brought to the same reference year.
By multiplying the original costs by a cost index ratio, the cost for the reference year can
be calculated, see Eq (2.64) [7].
Cost in reference year = Original cost
(Cost index in reference year)
(Cost index when the cost was obtained)
(2.64)
The cost index is an inﬂation indicator which corrects the PEC of an equipment so it
matches the reference year. In this thesis, the ”Chemical Engineering Plant Cost Index”
(CEPCI) has been used. As the average CEPCI for year 2019 has not been published yet,
the average CEPCI for 2018 has been used as an alternative. For year 2018, the average
(CEPCI) is equal to 603,1 [29]. The used costs CPE,W, dimensions or sizes XW, scaling
exponents and CEPCI for the HP are listed in Table (2.8). It should be noticed that the
valves have been left out in the cost estimation. This is due to the fact that the costs of
valves is much lower than for a HEX, compressors and pumps.
Table 2.8: Original cost CPEC,W, size XW and scaling exponent γ used for the PEC. Here
HP and LP stand for high pressure and low pressure, respectively.

After the total PEC of the HP has been estimated, the ﬁxed capital investment (FCI)
which is the sum of the direct costs (DC) and indirect costs (IC), can be estimated by
Eq. (2.65).
FCI = 4, 30 · PEC
(2.65)
For a new HP system, TCI can be estimated by Eq. (2.66).
TCI = 6, 32 · PEC
(2.66)
The factor 4.30 in Eq. (2.65) and the factor 6.32 in Eq. (2.66) are both used as a rule
of thump to estimate FCI and TCI. After an HP has been designed and built, the real
value of FCI and TCI can vary widely compared to the estimated one due to unexpected
expenses.
48
==PAGE:64==
2.5
Sensitivity Analysis
In order to obtain a better understanding of the thermodynamically and economically best
performing DH conﬁguration, a sensitivity analysis is performed. The sensitivity analysis
will investigate how the COP, total DH area and total pump work change when ﬁve
variables are changed in a ±% range. The ﬁve variables are; HEX water channel velocity v,
length and width ratio L/W, plate corrugation angle β, pinch point temperature diﬀerence
∆Tpinch and ﬁnally, the wave-length and plate press depth ratio Λ/b. In Table (2.9), the
ﬁve variables together with their individual changing range are presented.
Table 2.9: Range of variables used in the sensitivity analysis of the COP, total DH area
ADH and total pump work ˙Wpump.
Variable
Range [%]
v
±80%
L/W
±80%
β
±60%
∆Tpinch
±70%
Λ/b
±30%
The origin of the sensitivity analysis will be the variable setting which provided the
best DH conﬁguration.
The setting will be varied regarding the speciﬁed range, and
the change in COP, total DH area and total pump work from the starting point will be
monitored along the y-axis.
By understanding the inﬂuence of the variables used in the thermodynamical model,
it is more clear which variables should be chosen for independence in the optimization of
the COP in the best DH conﬁguration.
49
==PAGE:65==
Chapter 3
Results
This chapter is dedicated to the results obtained in the thesis. The results are the product
of the theory described in the method section. First, the chapter will present the results
obtained from the validation of the condenser and evaporator EES codes. Then the results
from the comparison between the diﬀerent DH conﬁgurations with PHEX and SPHEX
will follow. Afterwards an economic evaluation of the best performing DH conﬁguration
of PHEX and SPHEX will be presented. Now also a sensitivity analysis will be presented,
where the geometry and internal condition of the HEX will be varied and studied for the
best thermodynamical and economical DH conﬁguration. Finally, the results from the
sensitivity analysis will be used to optimize the COP. The EES codes used for the result
section are presented in the Appendix (D).
3.1

During the thesis study, the EES codes of the condenser and evaporator of PHEX and
SPHEX were validated against data from real components. The PHEX condenser code
and PHEX evaporator code were evaluated against an Alfa Laval ”TK20BW” condenser
and an ”MK15BW” evaporator. The results from the validation are presented in Table
(3.1).

3.2
Comparison of DH Conﬁgurations
From the simulation of the diﬀerent DH combinations, several results were obtained. The
thermodynamic state points for this section are given in Appendix (A). In order to give
a better picture showing how the large-scale ammonia HP works, log P-h diagrams are
created. In Figure (3.1) a log P-h diagram of Design 1 is presented.
Figure 3.1: Log P-h diagram of Design 1. The number indicates the thermodynamic state
points. The green line indicate HP 1 and the red line indicate HP 2.
In Figure (3.1) the pressure and speciﬁc enthalpy for the state points in Design 1 are
given. The green line indicates the lower HP 1 and the red line indicates the upper HP 2
in Design 1. In the diagram, heat is transferred to the DH network between state point
4 −5 −6 −7 for HP 1 and between state point 16 −17 −18 −19 for HP 2. Additionally,
it can be seen that HP 2 has a higher condenser and intermediate pressure than HP 1.
As the working pressure is higher in HP 2, the power input to compressor 3 and 4 (state
point 13 −14 and 15 −16) is greater than the power input to compressor 1 and 2 (state
point 1 −2 and 3 −4).
52
==PAGE:68==
By applying the two desuperheaters (DSHL and DSHH) after compressor 1 and 3, re-
spectively and rearranging the DH piping network over the heat sink, Design 2 is obtained.
In Figure (3.2) a Log P-h diagram of Design 2 is presented.
Figure 3.2: Log P-h diagram of Design 2. The number indicates the thermodynamic state
points. The green line indicate HP 1 and the red line indicate HP 2.
In Figure (3.2) the pressure and speciﬁc enthalpy for the state points in Design 2 are
given. In the diagram, heat is transferred between state point 2 −DSHL1 and 4−5−6−7
for HP 1 and between stat point 14 −DSHH1 and 16 −17 −18 −19 for HP 2. Again the
upper HP 2 has a higher condenser and intermediate pressure than HP 1 which means
that the power input to compressor 3 and 4 is larger than the power input to compressor
1 and 2.
To give a more profound explanation how heat is transferred from the HP to the
the DH network, TQ diagrams of Design 1 and Design 2 are created. In Figure (3.3)
a TQ-diagram for Design 1 with a pinch point temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch of 5 K is
presented.
53
==PAGE:69==
Figure 3.3: TQ-diagram of Design 1. The diagram is created for a pinch point temperature
diﬀerence of 5 K. The solid lines represent the refrigerant side and the dashed line represent
the DH water.
In Figure (3.3) it can be seen how the DH water is heated from TDH2 to TDH9 by
receiving heat from the condenser unit 1 and the condenser unit 2. It should be noticed
that condenser unit 2 has the highest HEX temperature (T16) in the TQ-diagram. As
condenser unit 2 has the highest temperature, the HEX component is exposed to the
highest thermal stresses.
54
==PAGE:70==
In Figure (3.4) a TQ-diagram of Design 2 is presented.
Figure 3.4: TQ-diagram of Design 1. The diagram is created for a pinch point temperature
diﬀerence of 5 K. The solid lines represent the refrigerant side and the dashed line represent
the DH water.
In Figure (3.4) it can be seen how the DH water is heated from TDH2 to TDH9 by re-
ceiving heat from from the desuperheater DSHL, condenser unit 1, desuperheater DSHH
and condenser unit 2. By utilizing the two desuperheaters, it is seen that the heat trans-
ferred from condenser unit 1 and condenser unit 2 becomes smaller. Moreover, by utilizing
the heat after the two compressors, the heat transfer area in condenser unit 1 and con-
denser unit 2 becomes reduced. The condenser unit 2 is still the HEX component which
is exposed to the highest temperature (T16) and hereby the largest thermal stresses.
By applying PHEX and SPHEX to Design 1 and Design 2 and using the heat transfer
correlations and pressure drop correlations plus the plate geometry range and the HEX
water channel velocity of 0,25 m/s, the power, COP and total DH pressure drop of each
of the four DH combinations can be calculated, see Table (3.3).

In Table (3.3) it can be seen that Design 1 has a compressor load ˙Wcomp of 1677 kW
and a COP of 2,989 when no HEX type is applied. After an HEX type is applied, the
COP decreases to 2,951 for Design 1 PHEX and 2,946 for Design 1 SPHEX. The reason
why the COP is greater for Design 1 PHEX is that Design 1 PHEX has a 0,0472 bar
smaller pressure drop over the DH heat sink which results in a 3,07 kW smaller pump
power than Design 1 SPHEX.
By adding the two desuperheaters DSHL and DSHH to the HP cycle, the heat load of
condenser unit 1 and condenser unit 2 decreases to 2348 kW and 2350 kW, respectively.
By doing so, the total compressor work for Design 2 decreases to 1581 kW which is 5, 72%
less than Design 1. By utilizing the two desuperheaters, the COP increases to 3,163 for
Design 2. After HEX type is applied to Design 2 the COP decreases to 3,130 for Design
2 PHEX and 3,123 for Design 2 SPHEX. The reason why the COP of Design 2 PHEX
is greater is that the total DH pressure drop over the heat sink is 0,0706 bar less for
Design 2 PHEX, and hereby the total pump power is 3, 11 kW smaller. By increasing
the complexity of Design 1 to Design 2, the COP increases by 5, 5%. By increasing the
complexity from Design 1 PHEX to Design 2 PHEX, the COP increases by 5, 72%, and
ﬁnally by increasing the complexity from Design 1 SPHEX to Design 2 SPHEX, the COP
increases by 5, 67%.

Figure 3.5: Pressure drop contributions from the diﬀerent HEXs.
In Figure (3.5), the pressure drops in condenser unit 1, condenser unit 2, DSHL and
DSHH are presented as a histogram. From Figure (3.5) it can be seen that the largest
pressure drops occur on the DH water side of the HEX. Moreover, it can be seen that
the refrigerant and water pressure drops in HP 1 are greater than the refrigerant and
water pressure drops for HP 2. However, one exception is Design 2 PHEX, where the
water pressure drop of HP 2 is slightly higher than the water pressure drop of HP 1.
When the complexity of the DH conﬁguration increases, the pressure drop decreases for
the refrigerant and water side. Subsequently, it can be seen that the pressure drops of
SPHEX than PHEX are higher, which makes the PHEX more preferable.
By looking only at the histogram, it is clear that that the pressure drop of the HEX
waterside must be the most important pressure drop because it is greatest. This means
that the water pressure drop is most important when pumps are included in the thermo-
dynamic model. If pumps are not included in the model, the water pressure drop becomes
less important for the cycle.
From Table (3.3) it is seen that the COP values of the diﬀerent DH combinations of
PHEX and SPHEX are very close to each other. Even though the COP values are close,
is it not the case when it comes to the geometry and heat transfer area of the diﬀerent DH
combinations. In Table (3.4) the plate dimensions (length and width L x W for PHEX
and diameter D for SPHEX), total plate No. n, heat transfer area A and overall heat
transfer coeﬃcients U, are presented for the HEXs used in the four DH combinations.

==PAGE:74==
From Table (3.4) it can be seen that Design 1 PHEX has a combined DH area of
165, 95 m2 whereas Design 1 SPHEX has a combined DH area of 224, 3 m2. This means
that Design 1 PHEX uses 26,01% less heat transfer area than Design 1 SPHEX. Table
(3.4) moreover shows that Design 2 PHEX has a combined DH area of 196, 86 m2 whereas
Design 2 SPHEX has a combined DH area of 270, 21 m2. This means Design 2 PHEX
uses 27,15% less heat transfer area than Design 2 SPHEX. The reason why the DH area
is smaller of a design using a PHEX is that the overall heat transfer coeﬃcient in general
is higher for a PHEX than a SPHEX.
For a condensation refrigerant, the heat transfer coeﬃcient should be within the range
of 1,0 kW/(m2·◦C) to 5,0 kW/(m2·◦C) and for a boiling refrigerant, the heat transfer
coeﬃcient should be within the range of 0,2 kW/(m2·◦C) to 5,0 kW/(m2·◦C) [12]. The
heat transfer coeﬃcients in the Table (3.4) lie within the speciﬁed range and can thereby
be seen as plausible values for the EES models.
It should be noticed that when the two desuperheaters are applied to Design 2, the
combined DH area increases. This results in the overall heat transfer coeﬃcient decreases
of the desuperheater zone, condenser zone and subcooling zone in the heat sink. This can
be seen in Design 1 PHEX condenser unit 1 where Ucond is equal to 4, 303 kW/(m2·◦C)
which decreases to 4, 256 kW/(m2·◦C) in Design 2 PHEX, which is equal to a reduction
of approximately 1,1%. The extra heat transfer area in the heat sink reduces the needed
heat transfer area in evaporator 1 and evaporator 2. This can be seen in Design 1 PHEX
for evaporator 1, where the area A is equal to 633, 7 m2 which decreases to 594, 3 m2 in
Design 2 PHEX, which is equal to a 6, 22% reduction.
By looking only at the results from condenser unit 1, it can be seen that Design 1
PHEX uses 389 plates whereas Design 1 SPHEX uses 224 plates, which are 165 plates
less. The reason that fewer plates are used for a SPHEX is that the plate dimension
for Design 1 PHEX is larger than Design1 SPHEX. The same plate tendency is seen for
Design 2 PHEX and Design 2 SPHEX. Additionally, the same tendency can be seen in
the evaporator of PHEX and SPHEX.
To this point Design 2 PHEX has thermodynamically and geometrically performed
best. Moreover, the PHEX plates have also shown to have a smaller pressure drop than
SPHEX. However, when choosing a design of a heat exchanger conﬁguration for heat pump
for district heating, the cost of the components must also be taken into consideration.
59
==PAGE:75==
3.3
Result from the Economic Evaluation
During the thesis study, the best performing DH conﬁguration of PHEX and SPHEX
were evaluated economically against each other. In the economic study, the purchase
equipment costs PEC, ﬁxed capital investment FCI and total capital investment TCI
were calculated for the best thermodynamic and geometrically performing design. From
Table (3.3) and Table (3.4) it is seen that Design 2 PHEX and Design 2 SPHEX is
performing best thermodynamically and geometrically. The economic result from Design
2 PHEX and SPHEX are presented in Table (3.5) and Table (3.6), respectively.
From Table (3.5) it can been seen that Design 2 PHEX has a total PEC of ¤ 661.801,36
and a FCI of ¤ 2.845.745,87 and a TCI of ¤ 4.182.584,62. However, from Table (3.6)
it can be sen that Design 2 SPHEX has a total PEC of ¤ 733.159,73 and a FCI of
¤3.152.586,85 and a TCI of ¤ 4.633.569,51. The TCI is hereby 9, 73% greater for Design
2 SPHEX than Design 2 PHEX.

COP value 3,130 of Design 2 PHEX. The zero point of the variable ranges are; velocity
= 0,25 m/s, L/W = 1, β = 30◦, ∆Tpinch = 5 K and Λ/b = 6.

Figure 3.6: Sensitivity analysis of the COP versus change in variables.
In Figure (3.6) it can be seen that when the water channel velocity is increased by
80%, the COP of the HP decreases by 1, 76%. When increasing the length and width
ratio L/W by 80%, the COP decreases by less than 1%. When the corrugation angle β
is decreased by 60%, the COP decreases by 7, 27%. If the corrugation angle instead is
increased by 60%, the COP value increases only by 0, 38%. Changes in the wavelength
and plate press depth ratio Λ/b has almost no noticeable eﬀect on the COP value. It
should be noticed that changes in the pinch point temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch has the
largest eﬀect on the COP value. By decreasing the pinch point temperature diﬀerence by
70%, the COP increases by 6, 26%, whereas a 70% increment results in a 7, 41% decrease
of the COP.

Figure 3.7: Sensitivity analysis of the DH area versus change in variables.
From Figure (3.7) it can be seen that when the water channel velocity is increased by
80%, the DH area decreases by 40, 62%. When the water channel velocity is decreased
by 80%, the DH area increases by 61, 62%. An increase and decrease of the length and

seen that when the corrugation angle β increases by 60%, the DH area increases by
24, 70%.
It should be noticed that the corrugation angle β is the only variable that
contributes negatively to the DH area when it is increased. When increasing the pinch
point temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch by 70%, the DH area decreases by 23, 83%. If ∆Tpinch
is decreased by 70%, the DH area is incremented by 65, 64%. Finally, it can be seen
that when the wavelength and plate press depth ratio is increased by 30%, the DH area
decreases by 6, 17%.

Figure 3.8: Sensitivity analysis of the pump power ˙Wpump versus change in variables.
In Figure (3.8), it can be seen that changes in the water channel velocity has the
greatest inﬂuence on the total pump power. When the water channel velocity is decreased
by 80%, it results in a 343, 45% reduction of the total pump power.
However, if the
velocity is increased by 80%, it results in a 63, 09% increment of the total pump power.
By incrementing the length and width ratio L/W by 80%, the total pump work increases
by 15, 40%. Moreover, it can be seen that the corrugation angle β has a sinusoidal behavior
along the x-axis. When the corrugation angle is increased or decreased by 60%, it results in
a decrement of 56, 98% and an increment of 87, 61% in the total pump power, respectively.
Additionally, Figure (3.8) shows that when the pinch point temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch
is incremented by 70%, the total pump power decreases by 25, 95%. Finally, the wave-
length and plate press depth ratio Λ/b has a local minimum at 0 variation of the variable.
If the ratio is increased or decreased, it results in a gain of 5, 83% and a gain of 6, 48% in
the total pump power, respectively. It should be noticed that the water channel velocity,
length and width ratio L/W, wave-length and plate press depth ratio Λ/b are the only
three variables the increment of which have a negative inﬂuence of the total pump power.

area increases as a result. Moreover, it can be seen that the lower the velocity in the
water channel is, the higher is the DH area. When the corrugation angle is between 20◦
to 55◦, the DH area is more or less constant for the velocity range of 0,3 m/s to 0,5 m/s.
