the inlet temperature for condenser unit 1. If the pinch point temperature is reduced, it
means that the compressor shall provide a less temperature and hereby pressure, which
results in an increment in the COP of the HP.
As the water channel velocity v, plate corrugation angle β and pinch point temperature
diﬀerence ∆Tpinch had the largest inﬂuence on the COP value, they are chosen to be
independent variables in the COP optimization. The built-in variable metric method in
EES is used for the COP optimization. In the optimization, the pinch point temperature
diﬀerence ∆Tpinch is varied in the range of 2 K to 5 K. The corrugation angle is varied in
the range of 15◦to 85◦, and the velocity is varied in the range of 0,2 m/s to 0,8 m/s. The
results of the COP optimization are listed in Table (3.7).

==PAGE:87==
Chapter 4
Discussion
The HP is a great technology which may solve Denmark’s future energy goals. When
the HP is combined with a low-temperature heat source and a DH network, it becomes a
great candidate. In section (2.1) Conﬁguration of Design 1 and 2, two DH conﬁgurations
were presented. Each HP conﬁguration utilizes low-temperature sea water as heat source
and uses the DH network at Sjællandsbroen as a heat sink.
Seawater is a great and almost unlimited energy source for the HP. However, there
are risks connected in using sea water as energy heat source. Over the year, the seawater
temperature in Copenhagen ﬂuctuates. This means that the HP will be exposed to a
water temperature close to 0◦C during winter times. The closer the sea water comes to
the freezing point, the greater is the risk of ice formation on the evaporator. In Sweden,
they have solved the problem by irrigating the evaporator with hot water [32]. But it
requires energy to do so which may decrease the COP of the HP. The Swedish people also
have the option to use water from the bottom of deep lakes. The water from the deep
lakes has a more uniform temperature during the year which reduces the ice formation
on the evaporators.
In Denmark, we do not have deep lakes. The solution will therefore be to irrigate
the evaporator during winter time or shut down the HP when the seawater temperature
approaches 0◦C. Instead, the DH water can be heated with an electric heater which is
directly coupled to the DH network. Even though the HP has some challenges regarding
the seawater temperature, it still has a great potential for solving Denmark’s future energy
goals.
4.1
The Conﬁguration of Design 1 and 2
In section (2,1) Conﬁguration of Design 1 and 2, two PI-diagrams were presented of Design
1 and Design 2. On the PI-diagrams, it can be seen that condenser unit 1 and condenser
unit 2 are divided into a desuperheater, condenser and subcooler HEX. However, in the
EES simulation, the three individual HEXs were modeled as a single unit. This approach
has led to complications regarding the HEX pressure drop calculations. In order to calcu-
late the pressure drop of each HEX, the individual length of the desuperheater, condenser
and subcooler must be calculated, see section (2.2.9) Pressure Drop in Heat Exchanger.
The provided heat transfer area for condenser unit 1 and condenser unit 2 in the Table
72
==PAGE:88==
(3.4) is therefore the total heat transfer area of the respective HEXs. If the three HEXs
had been modeled separately, it would result in three HEXs having each their own plate
dimension. This is due to fact that the pressure drop is not uniform through the condenser
unit.
In the design of the two DH conﬁgurations, reciprocating compressors were chosen.
By using reciprocating compressors instead of dynamic compressors, no oil separators and
HEX for oil cooling are needed. The HP becomes more simple in design and hereby less
expensive as fewer components are needed.
4.2
Validation of EES Condenser and Evaporator Code
From the validation of the EES condenser and evaporator code, it was seen that most of
the heat transfer areas and pressure drops estimations for ammonia and water were within
reasonable result ranges. However, three results from the SPHEX condenser and SPHEX
evaporator where deviating with a least ±80%. The ﬁrst result is the pressure drop for
R717 in the SPHEX condenser which had a deviation of 80% compared to Vahterus. The
second result is the heat transfer area in the SPHEX evaporator which had a deviation
of 83, 52% compared to Vahterus. The last result is the pressure drop for the R717 in
the SPHEX evaporator which had a deviation of −92, 31% compared to Vahterus. One
reason for these ﬂuctuating values is the applied correlations of the heat transfer area
and pressure drop. The data sheets in the Appendix (B) do not provide any information
regarding which correlation Alfa Laval or Vahterus have used. In order to apply reasonable
correlations, the correlations found in the literature study have been applied. After the
simulations of diﬀerent DH conﬁguration were performed, it was found out that there was
an error in the used condenser correlation created by ”Yan and Lin (1999)”. The error
resulted in an underestimation of the heat transfer area. It could therefore be interesting
to apply an alternative correlation to the EES code in order to see whether the validation
is still within reasonable result ranges or alternative correlations should be used in order
to obtain a plausible condenser and evaporator in the EES code. This can be investigated
in a further analysis.
4.3
Comparison of DH Conﬁgurations
From the result of the evaluation of the DH conﬁgurations, it was seen that by increasing
the complexity of the DH conﬁgurations, the COP increased as a result. Moreover, it
was seen that PHEX was performing geometrically better than SPHEX because it used
a smaller DH area for the heat transfer to the DH water.
One reason why the PHEX uses a smaller heat transfer area for the DH is the way
that the mass ﬂux G has been modeling in the EES code. For the PHEX, the mass
ﬂux has been calculated from a cross-section which has been calculated by a uniform
width W times the plate press depth b times number of ﬂuid channels nfluid, whereas the
SPHEX mass ﬂux has been calculated from a cross section calculated by a uniform plate
diameter Dp times the plate press depth b times the number of ﬂuid channels nfluid, see
section (2.2.5) Mass Flux of the HEX Channels. As the mass ﬂux of the SPHEX has not
73
==PAGE:89==
been calculated in a way that matches its circular geometry, it has resulted in a larger
cross section. Had a varying width instead been used for the SPHEX, it would result in
a smaller plate cross-section and hereby a larger mass ﬂux through the HEX. A larger
mass ﬂux would result in a greater Reynolds’s No. and a better chance for obtaining a
turbulent ﬂuid. A larger Reynolds’s No. would additionally increase the heat transfer
coeﬃcient and hereby would a smaller DH area be needed for the SPHEX. The total DH
heat transfer area for the SPHEX presented in Table (3.4) is therefore smaller in reality.
In the Table (3.4) it can also be seen that the PHEX plates have an equal length and
width dimension. This is due to the fact that the length and width ratio L/W is equal
to 1. The reason why the ratio of 1 is chosen, is that the EES code converged best for
this value. In reality, the length is often greater than the width. In Design 2 PHEX,
plate dimension of 0,090 m x 0,090 m and a plate dimension of 0,089 m x 0,089 m were
calculated for the DSHL and the DSHH, respectively. This resulted in 1785 plates of
desuperheater DSHL and 1853 plates of the desuperheater DSHH. The plate numbers
are unrealistic and so larger plate dimension with more channels would be preferred even
though it would increase the pressure drop of the units.
From the investigation of the pressure drop from the diﬀerent HEXs, see histogram
(3.5) it was seen that the water pressure drop was largest and hereby the most important
for the cycle. However, if pumps are not included in the thermodynamic model, the water
pressure drop becomes less important for the model.
In the EES model, the pressure drop of the compressors, pumps, valves and pipes
have been neglected. Therefore the COP stated in the Table (3.3) is in fact smaller in
reality because a larger work input to pumps and compressors are needed. As the same
assumptions are made for all the DH conﬁgurations, the result regarding the COP and
heat transfer area is still valid for use in the comparison of the DH conﬁgurations.
4.4
Economic Evaluation
From the economic evaluation, it was seen that Design 2 PHEX had the lowest total PEC,
FCI and TCI. One reason why Design 2 SPHEX was 9, 73% more expensive than Design 2
PHEX was that condenser unit 1 and condenser unit 2 in Design 2 SPHEX were 22, 96%
and 22, 38% more expensive than the PHEX condenser units used in Design 2 PHEX.
Another reason why Design 2 SPHEX was more expensive was that the heat transfer area
of all the SPHEX components is larger than that of the the PHEX components. The
extra heat transfer area of the SPHEX means the HEXs contain a much larger refrigerant
charge. A greater refrigerant charge of the HP does not directly have a big inﬂuence in
the TCI calculation. However, due to the extra refrigerant charge, the separator and open
ﬂash intercooler volume must be increased signiﬁcantly which results in higher cost prices.
Hereby separator 1 and 2 were 17, 33% and 18, 63% more expensive in Design 2 SPHEX,
and intercooler 1 and 2 were 18, 66% and 17, 96% more expensive in Design 2 SPHEX.
It can moreover be discussed how plausible the calculated PEC values for the economic
estimation is. First of all, the PEC has been calculated to the present value of year 2018.
This is due to the fact that the CEPCI of year 2019 is not available yet. Had a CEPCI for
year 2019 been used instead, it would result in larger values in the Table (3.5) and Table
(3.6) because of inﬂation between the year 2018 and 2019. Moreover, the six-tenth rule is
74
==PAGE:90==
applied for all the cost scaling exponents for the SPHEX components. The reason for this
is that not much information regarding the exponent value is available in the literature
as the SPHEX is a relatively new HEX type. As the exponent is larger for the SPHEX,
the TCI for PHEX HEX type becomes more favorable.
4.5
Sensitivity Analysis and COP Optimization
From the sensitivity analysis, several geometric and thermodynamic variables were stud-
ied. In the sensitivity analysis of the COP, it was seen that the pinch point temperature
diﬀerence ∆Tpinch, corrugation angle β and HEX water channel velocity of the water side
had the greatest inﬂuence, see Figure (3.6). When the pinch point temperature diﬀerence
decreased by 70%, the COP increased signiﬁcantly by 6, 26%. The reason is: when the
∆Tpinch value decreases, a smaller temperature and pressure value at the condenser inlet
are needed, see Figure (3.13). When the condenser pressure decreases, so does the needed
compressor power, and the COP of the cycle increases as a result. When the corruga-
tion angle β was decreased by 60%, the COP decreased by 7, 27%. The reason why the
corrugation angle β has a big inﬂuence on the COP is that when the corrugation angle
decreases, the path of the ﬂuid particle inside the HEX becomes longer. A longer ﬂuid
path increases the pressure drop of the HEX and the pump must hereby pay a larger
power input to the HP cycle which then lowers the COP value, see Figure (3.9). When
the water channel velocity increased by 80%, the COP decreased by 1, 76%. The reason
is that at a smaller channel velocity, more HEX plates are needed for transferring the
heat to the DH water. When the plate number increases, so does the port pressure drop,
see Eq. (2.55). When the pressure drop increases, a larger power input is needed to the
compressors and the COP decreases. In the sensitivity analysis of the COP, the length
and width ratio L/W was also studied. It was seen that the COP increased slightly for
a smaller ratio. However, it does not make sense to reduce the ratio below 1. If the ratio
is less than 1, the width becomes longer than the length. Therefore the length and width
ratio which provides the best COP value is L/W equal to 1.
From the sensitivity analysis of the DH area, it was noticed that the pinch point
temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch, corrugation angle β and HEX channel velocity of the water
side had the largest inﬂuence on the total DH area, see Figure (3.7). When the pinch point
temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch increases by 70%, the DH area decreases by 23, 83%. The
reason why the DH area decreases when the pinch point temperature diﬀerence increases
can be found in Eq.(2.44). When the corrugation angle increases by 60%, the total DH
area increases by 24, 70%. The reason why the DH area increases when the corrugation
angle increases, is that at a higher corrugation angle β, the overall heat transfer coeﬃcient
U for each HEX zone decreases which means that a larger DH area is needed. When
the water channel velocity in the HEX increases by 80%, the total DH area decreases
by 40, 62%. The reason why the DH area is reduced when the water channel velocity
increases, is that at a higher velocity, a higher heat transfer coeﬃcient is obtained. The
higher heat transfer coeﬃcient reduces the needed DH area. From Figure (3.7) it was
furthermore seen that changes in the length and width ratio L/W created almost no
change in the DH area. Subsequently, it was noticed that the corrugation angle β was
the only variable which increased the DH area when it was incremented. Finally, the
75
==PAGE:91==
wave-length and plate press depth ratio Λ/b did also have a great inﬂuence. However, the
EES code was very sensitive to changes of this ratio, which made the code crash if the
ratio was increased or decreased by more than ±30%.
In the sensitivity analysis of the total pump power ˙Wpump, it was seen that changes in
the water channel velocity had the greatest inﬂuence on the pump power, see Figure (3.8).
When the water channel velocity was decreased by 80%, the pump power decreased by
343, 45%, whereas if the water channel velocity was increased by 80% it only incremented
the pump work by 63, 09%. The reason why the total pump power increases when the
velocity increases is that at higher velocity, greater mass ﬂux exists. The greater mass
ﬂux increases the pressure drop of the HEX, see Eq.(2.55), Eq. (2.56) and Eq. (2.59),
which means that the power input to the pump must increase as well.
From the optimization part, it was found out that there was a trade-oﬀbetween a
large COP or a small DH area. By using the three variables; water channel velocity,
corrugation angle β and pinch point temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch, which had the most
inﬂuence on the COP in the sensitivity analysis, a COP optimization was performed.
For the corrugation angle of 53, 67◦, a velocity of 0,2 m/s and a pinch point temperature
of 2, 0 K, a maximum COP of 3,368 was obtained. The COP value was an increment
of 7, 07% compared to Design 2 PHEX. However, the DH area increased radically to
455, 36 m2 which was equal to an increment of 56, 77% compared to Design 2 PHEX.
If instead the DH area was minimized, it was found out that for a corrugation angle
of 53, 66◦, a velocity of 0,8 m/s and a pinch point temperature diﬀerence of 2,037 K, a
COP value of 3,240 was obtained, which was equal to an increment of 3, 4% compared
to Design 2 PHEX. Moreover, the DH area was calculated to 193, 48 m2 which was equal
to a reduction of 1, 72% compared to Design 2 PHEX. For this setting, the TCI becomes
¤3.751.756 which was 10, 3% smaller than the TCI for Design 2 PHEX.
From the COP optimization and DH area minimization it was additionally found
out that a similar corrugation angle of approximately 53◦and pinch point temperature
diﬀerence of approximately 2 K provides the best COP and smallest DH area, for the
speciﬁed independent variable range. However, if the water channel velocity was increased
for the settings obtained from the DH area minimization, it led to the result that the COP
increased even more, but in return on expenses on the DH area and hereby the TCI.
76
==PAGE:92==
Chapter 5
Conclusion
From the thesis study, it can be concluded that it is possible to theoretically optimize
a heat exchanger conﬁguration for a 5 MW two-stage ammonia HP by increasing the
complexity of the DH conﬁguration and in the meantime varying the HEX type applied
to the system.
From the comparison of the DH conﬁgurations, it was seen that by increasing the
DH complexity from Design 1 PHEX to Design 2 PHEX, the COP value increased by
5, 72% and by increasing the DH complexity from Design 1 SPHEX to Design 2 SPHEX,
the COP value increased by 5, 67%. Moreover, by changing the applied HEX type from
SPHEX to PHEX, the DH area decreased by 26, 01% from Design 1 SPHEX to Design
1 PHEX, and by changing the applied HEX type from SPHEX to PHEX, the DH area
decreased by 27, 15% from Design 2 SPHEX to Design 2 PHEX. The main reason that
the DH area of the PHEX was smaller was that the overall heat transfer coeﬃcient of
the PHEX was greater than the heat transfer coeﬃcient of the SPHEX. Based on these
results, it can hereby be concluded that Design 2 PHEX has the largest COP value and
smallest DH area. Additionally, it can also be concluded that PHEX is more favorable
when only looking at the COP value and total DH area.
From the investigation of the diﬀerent pressure drops in the HEX components, it can
be concluded that SPHEX has a larger pressure drop than PHEX. Furthermore, it can be
concluded that the water-side of the HEX has the greatest pressure drop in the HP cycle.
It is hereby the water pressure drop which is the most important pressure drop factor for
the HP cycle when pumps are included in the model and the COP is estimated.
From the economic analysis, it was seen that the choice of HEX used in the DH
conﬁguration of the HP had a large eﬀect on the total capital investment. The TCI for
Design 2 PHEX was calculated to ¤ 4.182.584,6 and the TCI for Design 2 SPHEX was
calculated to ¤ 4.633.569,5 which is 9, 73% higher than Design 2 PHEX. It can hereby
be concluded that by using PHEX rather than SPHEX in the DH conﬁguration, the TCI
reduces as a result. Hereby the PHEX is the most suitable HEX solution to use for the
DH conﬁguration based on the economical study of the thesis.
From the sensitivity analysis of the PHEX, it can be concluded that the three variables
which have the greatest inﬂuence on the COP and DH area are; pinch point temperature
diﬀerence ∆Tpinch, corrugation angle β and HEX water channel velocity, whereas the
length and width ratio L/W has the smallest inﬂuence.
77
==PAGE:93==
From the optimization part of the COP, it can be concluded that the variable settings
providing the highest COP for Design 2 PHEX, is a corrugation angle β of 53, 67◦, a water
channel velocity of 0,2 m/s and a pinch point temperature diﬀerence of 2,0 K. By having
these three variable settings, the COP value becomes 3,368 which is 7, 07% higher than
the COP value of Design 2 PHEX. Moreover, the DH area becomes 455, 36 m2, which is
56, 77% larger than the DH area of Design 2 PHEX. The TCI of the COP optimization
becomes ¤ 5.016.788, which is 16, 63% higher than the TCI for Design 2 PHEX.
From the minimization of the DH area, it can be concluded that the settings of the
three variables which provide the smallest DH area of Design 2 PHEX, is a corrugation
angle β of 53, 66◦, a water channel velocity of 0,8 m/s and a pinch point temperature
diﬀerence of 2,037 K which results in a COP value of 3,240 which is 3, 4% higher than
the COP value of Design 2 PHEX. Moreover, the DH area becomes 193, 48 m2 which is
1, 72% smaller than the DH area of Design 2 PHEX. The TCI of the DH area minimization
becomes ¤ 3.751.756, which is 10, 3% smaller than the TCI of Design 2 PHEX.
As the DH area of the minimization part result in the lowest TCI value, it can hereby
be concluded that it is most favorable to optimize the 5 MW two-stage ammonia HP with
PHEX according to the stated variable settings from the DH area minimization part.
78

==PAGE:97==
Appendix A
State Points for the DH
Conﬁgurations
This section contains the thermodynamic state point results from EES for the diﬀerent
DH conﬁgurations with and without HEX applied. The thermodynamic values are created
for a pinch point temperature diﬀerence ∆Tpinch of 5 K, a corrugation angle β of 30◦, a
wavelength and plate press depth ratio Λ/b of 3 and a water channel velocity of 2,5 m/s.
For the PHEX is a length and width ratio L/W of 1 applied. On the following pages are
the state points presented for DH conﬁgurations in the following order; Design 1, Design
2, Design 1 PHEX, Design 1 SPHEX, Design 2 PHEX and Design 2 SPHEX.

Appendix B
Heat Exchanger Data Sheets
This appendix section contains the data sheets for the condenser PHEX and SPHEX and
evaporator PHEX and SPHEX evaluation. The PHEX condenser and evaporator are from
the Danish manufacturer Alfa Laval and the SPHEX condenser and evaporator are from
the Finish manufacturer Vahterus. On the following pages are the data sheets given in
the following order; PHEX condenser, PHEX evaporator, SPHEX condenser and SPHEX
evaporator.
89
==PAGE:105==
.
Alfa Laval TK20 W
Gasketed plate-and-frame heat exchanger for demanding applications
.
Alfa Laval Industrial semi-welded line is used when gaskets are
not suitable for one of the process media. The semi-welded
line can also withstand a higher design pressure compared to
fully gasketed plate-and-frame heat exchangers.
The relatively short plate makes this model suitable for duties
with short temperature programs and when a low pressure
drop is appreciated. A large range of plate and gasket types is
available.
Applications
•
Chemicals
•
Energy and Utilities
•
Food and Beverages
•
HVAC and Refrigeration
•
Marine and Transportation
•
Mining, Minerals and Pigments
•
Pulp and Paper
•
Steel
•
Water and Waste treatment
Benefits
•
High energy efficiency – low operating cost
•
Flexible configuration – heat transfer area can be modified
•
Easy to install – compact design
•
High serviceability – easy to open for inspection and
cleaning and easy to clean by CIP
•
Access to Alfa Laval’s global service network
Features
Every detail is carefully designed to ensure optimal
performance, maximum uptime and easy maintenance.

.
Alfa Laval M15
Gasketed plate-and-frame heat exchanger for a wide range of applications
.
Alfa Laval Industrial line is a wide product range that is used in
virtually all types of industry.
Suitable for a wide range applications, this model is available
with a large selection of plate and gasket types.
In addition to normal single plate configuration, this model is
also available with double wall plates. Double wall plates are
used as an extra precaution to avoid intermixing of fluids.

•

Procedure
lmtd (Thot;in; Thot;out; Tcold;in; Tcold;out; switch : Tlm)
The Function is called by: call  lmtd(Thot,in;T,hot,out;T,cold,in;T,cold,out;0 for parrel and 1 for counter flow:DELTATlm)
If  switch  = 0
  Then
For parrel flow
T1  := Thot;in  – Tcold;in
Delta 1 temp. diffrence
T2  := Thot;out  – Tcold;out
Delta 2 temp. diffrence
Else
For counter flow
T1  := Thot;in  – Tcold;out
Delta 1 temp. diffrence
T2  := Thot;out  – Tcold;in
Delta 2 temp. diffrence
EndIf
